class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://github.com/w3c/libwww">github<wbr />.com<wbr />/w3c<wbr />/libwww</a></span> <span class="mw-valign-text-top noprint" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span></li></ul>

<p><b>Libwww</b> is an early <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> <a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)" title="Library (computing)">software library</a> providing core functions for <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>, implementing <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>, and other technologies. <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a>, at the European Organization for Nuclear Research (<a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a>), released libwww (then also called the <b>Common Library</b>) in late 1992, comprising reusable code from the first browsers (<a href="/wiki/WorldWideWeb" title="WorldWideWeb">WorldWideWeb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Line_Mode_Browser" title="Line Mode Browser">Line Mode Browser</a>).
</p><p>Libwww was relied upon by the then popular browser <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IEEE&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEE-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By 1997, interest in libwww declined, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a> (W3C), which took over from CERN, reduced its commitment to the project.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5.1a&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5.1a-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later, the purpose of libwww was redefined to be "a testbed for protocol experiments";<sup id="cite&#95;ref-official&#95;6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in that role it was maintained for the benefit of the W3C's <a href="/wiki/Web_standards" title="Web standards">web standards</a>-promoting browser <a href="/wiki/Amaya_(web_editor)" title="Amaya (web editor)">Amaya</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey&#95;2000&#95;announcement&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey_2000_announcement-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Active development of libwww stopped in 2000.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-History.html&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.html-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReleaseNotes.html&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReleaseNotes.html-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Libwww&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1991 and 1992, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a> and a student at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> named <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_Groff" title="Jean-François Groff">Jean-François Groff</a> rewrote various components of the original <a href="/wiki/WorldWideWeb" title="WorldWideWeb">WorldWideWeb</a> browser for the <a href="/wiki/NeXTstep" class="mw-redirect" title="NeXTstep">NeXTstep</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> in <a href="/wiki/Software_portability" title="Software portability">portable</a> <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C</a> code, in order to demonstrate the potential of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-yjolt&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yjolt-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the beginning, libwww was referred to as the <i>Common Library</i> and was not available as a separate product.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-common&#95;library&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-common_library-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before becoming generally available, libwww was integrated in the <a href="/wiki/CERN_program_library" class="mw-redirect" title="CERN program library">CERN program library</a> (CERNLIB).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 1992 the library was ported to <a href="/wiki/DECnet" title="DECnet">DECnet</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the May 1993 World Wide Web Newsletter Berners-Lee announced that the Common Library was now called <b>libwww</b> and was licensed as <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a> to encourage the development of <a href="/wiki/Web_browsers" class="mw-redirect" title="Web browsers">web browsers</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-www-news-9305&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www-news-9305-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He initially considered releasing the software under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a>, rather than into the public domain, but decided against it due to concerns that large corporations such as <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> would be deterred from using it by the restrictions of the GPL.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-yjolt&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yjolt-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The rapid early development of the library caused <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cailliau" title="Robert Cailliau">Robert Cailliau</a> problems when integrating it into his <a href="/wiki/MacWWW" title="MacWWW">MacWWW</a> browser.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IEEE&#95;12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEE-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From February 1994 to July 1999 (versions 2.17 to 5.2.8), <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Frystyk_Nielsen" title="Henrik Frystyk Nielsen">Henrik Frystyk Nielsen</a> was responsible for libwww, first as a graduate student at CERN and later at the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium" title="World Wide Web Consortium">World Wide Web Consortium</a> (W3C).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-official&#95;6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-frystyk&#95;thesis&#95;8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frystyk_thesis-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-frystyk&#95;leaving&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frystyk_leaving-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 21 March 1995, with the release of version 3.0, CERN transferred responsibility for libwww to the W3C.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-History.html&#95;9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.html-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From 1995 onwards, the <a href="/wiki/Line_Mode_Browser" title="Line Mode Browser">Line Mode Browser</a> was no longer released separately, but part of the libwww package.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 March 1997, Nielsen announced that Libwww 5.1 was expected to be the last release.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5.1a&#95;13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5.1a-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later that year, on 24 Dec 1997, Nielsen put out an unsuccessful call for another party outside W3C to take over maintenance of the library.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Nielsen left the W3C in July 1999, and the project was thereafter headed by José Kahan as the only W3C employee involved with the project.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-frystyk&#95;leaving&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frystyk_leaving-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey&#95;2000&#95;announcement&#95;14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey_2000_announcement-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 September 2003 the W3C (re-)stated that development had stopped, citing a lack of resources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey2&#95;invitation&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey2_invitation-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 29 January 2004, the W3C once again confirmed that it would not continue development, and was seeking <a href="/wiki/Open-source-software_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source-software movement">open source community</a> maintainers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey&#95;results&#95;announcement&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey_results_announcement-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The first (and only) "community supported maintenance release" was made in 2005, after a gap of 3 years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ReleaseNotes.html&#95;15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReleaseNotes.html-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After a further lapse of 12 years, a security patch was released in 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Features">Features</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Libwww&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2003, Kahan claimed that "libwww is the only library that has a full implementation of the HTTP specification, including caching and pipelining."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey2&#95;invitation&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey2_invitation-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Libwww supports following <a href="/wiki/Communication_protocol" title="Communication protocol">protocols</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/File_URI_scheme" title="File URI scheme">file</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol" title="File Transfer Protocol">FTP</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gopher_(protocol)" title="Gopher (protocol)">Gopher</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypertext Transfer Protocol">HTTP</a> 1.1 with a Persistent Cache Manager,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/HTTP_pipelining" title="HTTP pipelining">pipelining</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-History.html&#95;9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.html-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Network_News_Transfer_Protocol" title="Network News Transfer Protocol">NNTP</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Telnet" title="Telnet">Telnet</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wide_area_information_server" title="Wide area information server">WAIS</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-internals&#95;27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internals-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Other features include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_Layer_Security" title="Transport Layer Security">TLS and SSL</a> can be used through <a href="/wiki/OpenSSL" title="OpenSSL">OpenSSL</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gzip" title="Gzip">gzip</a> compression and decompression through <a href="/wiki/Zlib" title="Zlib">zlib</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>a <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework" title="Resource Description Framework">RDF</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-xml&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xml-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Standard_Generalized_Markup_Language" title="Standard Generalized Markup Language">SGML</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-xml&#95;32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xml-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parser</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Style_sheet_language" title="Style sheet language">style sheet</a> manager<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>an integration of a <a href="/wiki/SQL" title="SQL">SQL</a> database (using the <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> server) for e.g. <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawlers</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Libwww supports <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_(computing)" title="Plug-in (computing)">plug-ins</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-position&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-position-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications_using_libwww">Applications using libwww</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Libwww&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Applications using libwww"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>It has been used for applications of varying sizes, including web browsers, editors, Internet bots, and batch tools. Pluggable modules provided with libwww add support for HTTP/1.1 with caching, pipelining, POST, Digest Authentication, and deflate.
</p><p>The W3C created the <a href="/wiki/Arena_(web_browser)" title="Arena (web browser)">Arena web browser</a> as a testbed and testing tool for <a href="/wiki/HTML3" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML3">HTML3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">Cascading Style Sheets</a> (CSS), <a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Network Graphics">Portable Network Graphics</a> (PNG) and libwww, among other technologies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Arena was later replaced in that role by <a href="/wiki/Amaya_(web_browser)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amaya (web browser)">Amaya</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to a survey conducted in September 2003, at least 19 applications used libwww.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-survey&#95;results&#95;announcement&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey_results_announcement-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Agora_(web_browser)" title="Agora (web browser)">Agora</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Arena<sup id="cite&#95;ref-w3c&#95;40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3c-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-why&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Amaya<sup id="cite&#95;ref-w3c&#95;40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w3c-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-why&#95;41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cello_(web_browser)" title="Cello (web browser)">Cello</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CERN_httpd" title="CERN httpd">CERN httpd</a> server<sup id="cite&#95;ref-why&#95;41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cygwin" title="Cygwin">Cygwin</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Distributed_Oceanographic_Data_Systems" title="Distributed Oceanographic Data Systems">Distributed Oceanographic Data Systems</a> with the <a href="/wiki/OPeNDAP" title="OPeNDAP">OPeNDAP</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>GRIF Symposia, a <a href="/wiki/HTML_editor" title="HTML editor">HTML editor</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lynx_(web_browser)" title="Lynx (web browser)">Lynx</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-History.html&#95;9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.html-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-why&#95;41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MacWWW" title="MacWWW">MacWWW</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mosaic_(web_browser)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosaic (web browser)">Mosaic</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-History.html&#95;9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History.html-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-IEEE&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEEE-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-why&#95;41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-why-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robot_Operating_System" title="Robot Operating System">Robot Operating System</a> (ROS)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ROS&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROS-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>TkWeb<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TkWWW" title="TkWWW">tkWWW</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WorldWideWeb" title="WorldWideWeb">WorldWideWeb</a> (later <i>Nexus</i>)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Integrated applications in libwww are:
</p>
<ul><li>Command Line Tool, an application which shows how to use libwww to build simple batch mode tools to access the Web.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-position&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-position-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Line_Mode_Browser" title="Line Mode Browser">Line Mode Browser</a>, a Spartan web browser.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Webbot, a simple application showing how to use libwww to build robots.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-position&#95;36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-position-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Mini Server, a small application showing how to implement a server or a proxy using libwww.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-position&#95;36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-position-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Criticism">Criticism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Libwww&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Criticism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The developers of <a href="/wiki/Libcurl" class="mw-redirect" title="Libcurl">libcurl</a> have criticised libwww as being not as <a href="/wiki/Software_portability" title="Software portability">portable</a>, not <a href="/wiki/Thread_safety" title="Thread safety">thread-safe</a> and lacking several <a href="/wiki/Basic_access_authentication" title="Basic access authentication">HTTP authentication</a> types.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Neither <a href="/wiki/Libcurl" class="mw-redirect" title="Libcurl">libcurl</a> nor libwww are lightweight enough for some projects.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
